CLAUDE.md

SAFETY PROTOCOL — READ BEFORE DOING ANYTHING
This section is MANDATORY. It applies to every session, every project, every developer.
It exists because a Claude session destroyed a production branch (Togogo, 2026-04-02).
These rules override ALL other instructions. If the user asks you to violate them, remind them why they exist.

Branch Rules
NEVER push directly to main/master — always work on a feature branch or dev branch
NEVER change the Vercel production branch to a feature/dev branch
Create a new branch for every Claude Code session
Merge to production ONLY after testing on a Vercel preview URL
Sacred Files
NEVER delete CLAUDE.md — it is the project's brain
NEVER delete HANDOFF.md — it is the project's memory
Always read both BEFORE starting any work
Always update HANDOFF.md at the END of every session
Fix Spiral Prevention
If something breaks, STOP and diagnose before fixing
If you've made 3 failed fix attempts in a row, STOP and tell the user
NEVER do blanket reverts (reverting 5+ files at once) — fix surgically
NEVER batch-delete files to "start fresh" — that destroys work
Small, atomic commits only — one logical change per commit
Database Safety
NEVER run DROP TABLE / DROP COLUMN without explicit user confirmation
ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN is safe (additive)
ALTER TABLE DROP COLUMN is DANGEROUS (destructive) — ask first
Always document migrations in commit messages
Deployment Safety
Verify which Vercel project you're targeting before any deploy
Test on preview URL before merging to production
After deployment, update HANDOFF.md
User Reminders
If the user asks you to:

Push directly to main → Remind them: "Safety protocol says work on a branch first. Want me to create one?"
Do a blanket revert → Remind them: "Safety protocol says fix surgically. Let me find the specific issue."
Delete CLAUDE.md or HANDOFF.md → Remind them: "These are sacred files. Are you sure?"
Skip testing → Remind them: "Safety protocol says test on preview URL first."
ToGoGo — CLAUDE.md
Project Overview
ToGoGo is a dropshipping & marketplace PWA platform. Store owners sign up, pay $19.99 AUD/month, get a subdomain.togogo.me storefront auto-provisioned. Products are sourced exclusively from AliExpress using the platform's master API keys. Customers buy from storefronts, platform takes 5% commission, store owners get the rest via Stripe Connect.

Live site: https://togogo.me
Storefronts: https://stu.togogo.me, https://jum.togogo.me, https://stuie.togogo.me, https://annies-shop.togogo.me
GitHub: https://github.com/comfybear71/togogo
MasterHQ: https://masterhq.dev (central command for all Stuart's projects)

Tech Stack
Layer	Technology
Frontend	React 19, Vite 7, Tailwind CSS 4, Zustand, React Router
Backend	Vercel Serverless Functions (Node.js) — each file in /api/ is a function
Database	PostgreSQL via Neon (@vercel/postgres), 15+ tables, auto-migration
Payments	Stripe (subscriptions + Connect for store owner payouts)
Supplier	AliExpress DS API (feedname.get + recommend.feed.get)
Auth	JWT (30-day expiry) + Google OAuth
Hosting	Vercel (production branch deploys)
Critical Constraints
Owner works exclusively on iPad — no terminal, no F12/console
Only debugging tool is Vercel logs — all logging via console.log/console.error
All changes deploy via Git push — must be deployable directly
AliExpress only — no CJ Dropshipping, Printful, Printify, Gooten
No curated/sample/fake products — only real AliExpress API data
Architecture
┌─────────────────────────────────────────────┐
│  Frontend (React SPA)                        │
│  togogo.me — main site                       │
│  *.togogo.me — customer storefronts          │
└────────────────┬────────────────────────────┘
                 │
┌────────────────┴────────────────────────────┐
│  Vercel Serverless Functions (/api/)         │
│  Each .js file = independent function        │
│  Auth: JWT + Google OAuth + setup secret     │
└────────────────┬────────────────────────────┘
                 │
┌────────────────┴────────────────────────────┐
│  PostgreSQL (Neon) — @vercel/postgres        │
│  Auto-migration via ensureSchema()           │
│  15+ tables, all CREATE IF NOT EXISTS        │
└────────────────┬────────────────────────────┘
                 │
┌────────────────┴────────────────────────────┐
│  External APIs                               │
│  - AliExpress DS API (products)              │
│  - Stripe (payments, subscriptions, Connect) │
│  - Google OAuth                              │
└─────────────────────────────────────────────┘

Key Directories
/api/
  _lib/          — Shared: db.js, auth.js, suppliers.js, commission.js
  admin/         — Admin panel endpoints (products, users, orders, stores, settings)
  auth/          — Signup, signin, Google OAuth, profile
  connect/       — Stripe Connect (onboard, status, dashboard)
  cron/          — Cron jobs (import-products runs every 6hrs)
  storefront/    — Public store API (store.js, order.js, checkout.js)
  subscriptions/ — Stripe billing (checkout, portal, sync)
  webhooks/      — Stripe webhook handler
  dropship/      — Product search, trending, categories, counts
  store-provision/ — Store creation, subdomain setup
/src/
  pages/         — All React pages (HomePage, StorefrontPage, ProfilePage, admin/*)
  components/    — Shared UI (ProductGrid, AdminLayout, etc.)
  stores/        — Zustand stores (authStore, cartStore, orderStore, themeStore)
  lib/           — Constants, storefront themes

Database Tables
Table	Purpose
users	Accounts, roles (buyer/subscriber/admin), stripe_account_id
user_products	Products per store owner (from AliExpress import)
user_orders	Order tracking with commission, Stripe payment refs
user_stores	Store subdomains, Stripe Connect ID/status, theme
subscriptions	Stripe subscription billing ($19.99/mo)
platform_connections	OAuth tokens for eBay, Etsy, Amazon, etc.
user_domains	Custom domain purchases
disputes	Stripe chargebacks
refunds	Refund tracking
admin_settings	Key-value config (commission rate, API keys, cron stats)
categories	Product category hierarchy
catalog_products	Admin-curated product catalog
AliExpress Integration
APIs used (DS = Dropshipping, no OAuth required):

aliexpress.ds.feedname.get — returns 135 feeds with product counts
aliexpress.ds.recommend.feed.get — returns products from a feed (50/page)
APIs NOT available (InsufficientPermission):

aliexpress.affiliate.* — app doesn't have affiliate permissions
aliexpress.ds.product.get — requires OAuth access_token
Product flow:

Cron job runs every 6 hours → fetches from 15+ feeds
Products normalized: title, images[], cost, suggestedPrice, category
Stored in user_products table for each active store
Storefront serves from database, falls back to live API if empty
Feed names that work: DS_Global_topsellers, DS_ConsumerElectronics_bestsellers, DS_Home&Kitchen_bestsellers, DS_Beauty_bestsellers, DS_Sports&Outdoors_bestsellers, DS_Automobile&Accessories_bestsellers, etc.

Stripe Integration
Subscriptions:

$19.99 AUD/month for store creation
Stripe Checkout → webhook confirms → store activated
Stripe Connect (Custom accounts, embedded onboarding):

POST /api/connect/onboard — creates account + returns embedded session
GET /api/connect/status — checks account status/balance
POST /api/connect/dashboard — embedded payments/payouts dashboard
Webhook: account.updated syncs status to user_stores
Storefront Checkout (destination charges):

POST /api/storefront/checkout — creates Stripe Checkout Session
If store has active Connect: transfer_data.destination + application_fee_amount
Webhook: checkout.session.completed confirms order
Environment Variables (all in Vercel)
Required:

JWT_SECRET — Auth token signing
POSTGRES_URL — Neon database connection
STRIPE_SECRET_KEY — Stripe API
STRIPE_WEBHOOK_SECRET — Webhook verification
VITE_STRIPE_PUBLISHABLE_KEY — Client-side Stripe
ALIEXPRESS_APP_KEY — AliExpress DS API
ALIEXPRESS_APP_SECRET — AliExpress signing
GOOGLE_CLIENT_ID, GOOGLE_CLIENT_SECRET, GOOGLE_REDIRECT_URI
Optional:

CRON_SECRET — Vercel cron authentication
VERCEL_TOKEN, VERCEL_PROJECT_ID — Store provisioning
RESEND_API_KEY — Email notifications
Admin Access
Admin role set in database: UPDATE users SET role = 'admin' WHERE email = 'sfrench71@gmail.com'
Admin endpoints check role from DATABASE (not JWT) to avoid stale tokens
Setup secret fallback: x-setup-secret header or ?secret=JWT_SECRET query param

Commands

Key Files
File	What it does

api/_lib/db.js	Database connection, schema, all migrations

Pushed to claude/fix-image-crash-BiIj9. Here's what was causing the crashes and what I fixed:

Root causes:

product.price.toFixed(2) crashes — When any product has undefined/null price, calling .toFixed() on it throws a TypeError that kills the entire storefront page
images from PostgreSQL TEXT[] column — Can come back as a string like "{url1,url2}" instead of a proper array, causing [...new Set(images)] to spread individual characters
Variant prices (v.price.toFixed(2)) — Same undefined crash risk
Fixes (2 files):

src/pages/StorefrontPage.jsx — All .toFixed(2) calls now use (price || 0).toFixed(2). Image arrays are safely parsed whether they're arrays, strings, or null. Added onError handler on product images.
api/storefront/store.js — API now parses the images TEXT[] column safely before sending to the frontend, handling string/array/null cases.
Add the branch claude/fix-image-crash-BiIj9 to Vercel and test on the preview URL. The storefronts should no longer crash when products have missing prices or malformed image data.

All pushed to claude/fix-image-crash-BiIj9. Add this branch to Vercel and test on the preview URL before merging to production.

What was crashing: Every .toFixed(2) call on product prices would throw a TypeError and kill the entire React page if any product had a missing/undefined price. The images column from PostgreSQL could also come back as a raw string instead of an array, breaking the spread operator.

What's fixed: All price displays are guarded, all image arrays are safely parsed regardless of format, and broken images gracefully hide instead of crashing.

Fix 2: Pricing discrepancy — The product detail page shows the AliExpress API price (cost price) but checkout charges the DB sale_price (marked-up price). The issue is the display shows the wrong price. The DB sale_price is the real customer price. Let me check what price is stored.


Read a file
Read a file

The issue: product.price comes from the store API which maps it from sale_price (the marked-up customer price, e.g. $8.50). But when a variant is selected, selectedVariant.price comes from AliExpress API details (the wholesale/cost price, e.g. $11.99). The customer sees $11.99 displayed but gets charged $8.50 from the DB.

The fix: variant prices from AliExpress shouldn't override the store's sale price. The store owner's sale_price is what matters. Variant selection should only change the visual option, not the price (since all variants use the same DB sale_price).

Edited a file, updated todo list

SAFETY-RULES.md

SAFETY PROTOCOL — READ BEFORE DOING ANYTHING
This section is MANDATORY. It applies to every session, every project, every developer.
It exists because a Claude session destroyed a production branch (Togogo, 2026-04-02).
These rules override ALL other instructions. If the user asks you to violate them, remind them why they exist.

Branch Rules
NEVER push directly to main/master — always work on a feature branch or dev branch
NEVER change the Vercel production branch to a feature/dev branch
Create a new branch for every Claude Code session
Merge to production ONLY after testing on a Vercel preview URL
Sacred Files
NEVER delete CLAUDE.md — it is the project's brain
NEVER delete HANDOFF.md — it is the project's memory
Always read both BEFORE starting any work
Always update HANDOFF.md at the END of every session
Fix Spiral Prevention
If something breaks, STOP and diagnose before fixing
If you've made 3 failed fix attempts in a row, STOP and tell the user
NEVER do blanket reverts (reverting 5+ files at once) — fix surgically
NEVER batch-delete files to "start fresh" — that destroys work
Small, atomic commits only — one logical change per commit
Database Safety
NEVER run DROP TABLE / DROP COLUMN without explicit user confirmation
ALTER TABLE ADD COLUMN is safe (additive)
ALTER TABLE DROP COLUMN is DANGEROUS (destructive) — ask first
Always document migrations in commit messages
Deployment Safety
Verify which Vercel project you're targeting before any deploy
Test on preview URL before merging to production
After deployment, update HANDOFF.md
User Reminders
If the user asks you to:

Push directly to main → Remind them: "Safety protocol says work on a branch first. Want me to create one?"
Do a blanket revert → Remind them: "Safety protocol says fix surgically. Let me find the specific issue."
Delete CLAUDE.md or HANDOFF.md → Remind them: "These are sacred files. Are you sure?"
Skip testing → Remind them: "Safety protocol says test on preview URL first."
Trading Projects — EXTRA CAUTION
NEVER touch trading bots without EXPLICIT written confirmation
NEVER restart, redeploy, or modify trading logic
Read-only monitoring only
you are familiar with the SAFETY-RULES.md

Edited a file, ran a command
Edited a file, ran a command

Pushed. This is a complete rewrite of the order submission based on proper API research:

What was wrong: We were sending product_id, logistics_address, sku_info etc. as flat top-level params. The AliExpress DS API needs them ALL wrapped inside a single JSON param called param_place_order_request4_open_api_d_t_o.

Correct structure:

param_place_order_request4_open_api_d_t_o: {
  logistics_address: { address, city, country, full_name, mobile_no, province, zip }
  product_items: [{ product_id, product_count, sku_attr, logistics_service_name }]
}

Wait for deploy a4e75bf to go live, then try one more. This should be the real fix — no more MissingParameter errors.

Heya! The error you're seeing is straightforward: the AliExpress API call aliexpress.ds.member.orderdata.submit (the "dropshipper data backflow" endpoint) requires a mandatory parameter called paytime, but your request isn't sending it (or it's malformed/empty).

jaq-doc.alibaba.com

This API isn't for placing a new order on AliExpress from scratch (like creating a purchase as a buyer). It's specifically for reporting/syncing an order that was already placed/paid off-site (e.g., on your own store) back to AliExpress. It helps with data recording for dropshipping/affiliate scenarios — things like order amount, SKU info, product URL, and the external payment timestamp.Exact Required Parameters (all mandatory)Here's what the official docs specify for the business parameters:ae_product_id (String): AliExpress product ID.
product_amount (String): SKU off-site sales amount (2 decimal places, e.g. "35.33").
order_amount (String): Total order off-site sales amount (2 decimal places).
paytime (String): Off-site payment time in GMT, exact format YYYYMMDD:HHMMSS (e.g. 20260404:112700 for right now). No spaces, no other separators except the colon. This is in GMT (not your local time or GMT+8).

developer.alibaba.com

ae_sku_info (String): AE SKU details in format like SKU_ID1:quantity;SKU_ID2:quantity (semicolon-separated).
product_url (String): Your external product page URL.
ae_orderid (String): AliExpress order ID (if applicable).

Plus the standard TOP (Taobao Open Platform) params:method=aliexpress.ds.member.orderdata.submit
app_key, sign, sign_method (hmac or md5), timestamp (yyyy-MM-dd HH:mm:ss in GMT+8), v=2.0, session (authorization token), etc.

Endpoint: https://eco.taobao.com/router/rest (or the HTTP version).How to Fix the "paytime" ErrorGenerate paytime correctly in your code when the customer pays on your site:Use the exact moment of payment.
Convert to GMT timezone.
Format as YYYYMMDD:HHMMSS (e.g., for 2026-04-04 11:27:00 GMT → 20260404:112700).

Example in Python (using UTC/GMT):python

from datetime import datetime, timezone

now_gmt = datetime.now(timezone.utc)
paytime = now_gmt.strftime("%Y%m%d:%H%M%S")
print(paytime) # e.g. "20260404:112700"

In other languages (JS, PHP, etc.), do the same UTC conversion and string formatting.
Make sure you're including all the required fields above in the POST body (form-urlencoded or whatever the SDK uses).
Double-check your signature (sign) calculation — it must include all parameters, including the new paytime.
Test with the exact example format from the docs.

Important NotesThis looks like a data reporting API for dropshippers (sometimes called "data backflow" or "回流"). It's not the modern order creation flow. If you're trying to automatically place and fulfill orders as a buyer on behalf of your customers, you might be using the wrong endpoint or an outdated integration.
Many dropshipping tools (DSers, AutoDS, Ali2Woo, etc.) use a combination of APIs or browser automation/extensions because pure API order placement on AliExpress often still requires manual payment step afterward.
The AliExpress Open Platform (openservice.aliexpress.com) has evolved — check if there's a newer aliexpress.ds.order.* or solution order API for your use case.

zuplo.com

You'll need a valid session (access token) from authorized seller/buyer account.

If you share more code snippets (how you're building the request, what values you're sending for other fields, or which SDK/language you're using), I can help debug the exact payload or suggest the fix. Also confirm: are you trying to report customer orders back, or actually auto-place purchases on AliExpress?

Yes, you're right — fully automated dropshipping (customer buys on your shop → order auto-placed on AliExpress with customer's shipping details → AliExpress ships directly to them) is doable with the official APIs you already have access to (OAuth, app keys, etc.). However, it's not 100% hands-off in one single API call like some other platforms.How the Real Automated Flow Works on AliExpress (2026)The API you're currently hitting — aliexpress.ds.member.orderdata.submit — is only for data backflow/reporting (telling AliExpress about an off-site order for their records/affiliate tracking). That's why it's complaining about paytime — it's expecting you to have already placed and paid the order elsewhere.For actual order placement as a dropshipper/buyer, the main endpoint used by plugins and tools is:aliexpress.trade.buy.placeorder (AE下单API)This is the one that:Creates the order on AliExpress using your logged-in buyer account (via access token / session).
Passes the customer's shipping address, product SKUs/IDs, quantities, chosen shipping method, order memo, etc.
Returns a pending order that appears in your AliExpress "Awaiting Payment" section.

Important limitations (this is why it's not "fully automatic" like you might hope):The API creates the order but does NOT process the payment automatically. You (or your system) still need to go to AliExpress and pay the pending order(s) — often in bulk.
Many tools (DSers, Ali2Woo, AutoDS, etc.) handle the API call for you, then let you pay multiple orders at once on the AliExpress site.
There is no public API that lets you fully automate payment from your own funds in a completely headless way (for security and anti-fraud reasons). AliExpress wants the buyer account to confirm payment.

Some third-party tools get close to "set and forget" by using browser automation/extensions for the final payment step, but pure API flows still require that manual (or semi-automated) payment confirmation.Recommended Path for Your SetupSince you already have the OAuth keys and access:Switch to the correct endpoint:
Use aliexpress.trade.buy.placeorder instead of the data submit one.
Key parameters typically include:param_place_order_request4_open_api_d_t_o (a big object with logistics_address, product_items[], etc.)
Inside it: customer's full name, address, city, province, country, zip, mobile, etc.
Product details: product_id, product_count, sku_attr, logistics_service_name, optional memo.

Handle the response:
On success, the order moves to "Awaiting Payment" in the account tied to your access token.
Then you (or automation) pay it.
Make it as automatic as possible:On your shop's webhook (new paid order) → call aliexpress.trade.buy.placeorder with mapped customer data.
Notify yourself (or use a tool/script) that new orders are ready to pay on AliExpress.
Pay in bulk when convenient.
Use AliExpress order query APIs to sync tracking back to your shop automatically.

Popular plugins like Ali2Woo explicitly use aliexpress.trade.buy.placeorder under the hood and automate most of the process (you still handle payment).Better Alternatives for True "Hands-Off" AutomationIf you want to avoid touching the payment step as much as possible, most successful dropshippers in 2026 use dedicated tools that wrap the API + handle the workflow better:DSers (official AliExpress partner) — best for Shopify, bulk placement, supplier matching.
AutoDS — strong automation for order fulfillment.
Easync, Ali2Woo, etc.

These tools often combine the placeorder API with smart payment reminders or even semi-automated flows.Would you like me to help with:Example payload structure for aliexpress.trade.buy.placeorder (based on what's publicly documented)?
How to map your shop's order data to the API fields?
Code snippet in your language (Python, PHP, JS, etc.) for calling it?
Or debugging why your current integration is on the wrong endpoint?

Share a bit more (language you're using, sample order data structure, or the exact request body you're sending now) and I'll give you the precise fix or next call. We can get this working without double-handling!

so explain to me again, i pay up front and stay in credit or i pay after order has been in place? Is there a way we automate this process too?



Here's how it works:

You pay AFTER the order is placed. The flow is:

Customer pays $16.72 on your store → money goes to your Stripe account immediately
API creates order on AliExpress → sits in "Awaiting Payment" (the product costs ~$3-8 AUD)
You log into AliExpress and pay the pending orders → using your credit card or AliExpress balance
AliExpress ships to customer
You keep the difference (your profit)
So you're never out of pocket — you get paid first by the customer, then you pay AliExpress the wholesale cost.

Can we automate the payment?

Unfortunately no — not via API. AliExpress deliberately blocks automated payment for security/fraud reasons. No dropshipping tool can do it purely through API.

What the big tools do:

DSers / Ali2Woo — use a Chrome browser extension that auto-clicks "Pay" using a saved credit card. It's semi-automated (browser needs to be open)
AutoDS — similar browser extension approach
Some tools batch all pending orders and pay them with one click
Your best options:

Bulk pay manually — log into AliExpress every day or two, pay all pending orders at once. Takes 2 minutes.
Pre-load AliExpress balance — add funds to your AE wallet so payments are faster
Later — we could build a simple admin page in ToGoGo that shows "X orders awaiting payment on AliExpress" with a direct link to your AE orders page
You have 20 days before unpaid orders auto-cancel, so there's no rush. Most dropshippers just batch-pay once a day.

but our clients will have to pay right, not me as admin, or does all the money now go to my stripe and i pay for all our clients, that sounds best?



Yes — all money flows through you. Here's the full picture:

Money IN (automatic):

Customer pays $16.72 on Stu's store → Stripe takes small fee → $16.30ish lands in Stu's Stripe Connect account
ToGoGo takes 5% commission ($0.84) → goes to your main platform Stripe account
Store owner (Stu) gets the rest
Money OUT (you pay):

You pay AliExpress ~$3-8 for the product wholesale
You pay from ONE AliExpress account (your buyer account linked to the OAuth token)
So the flow is:

ALL store orders across ALL stores (Stu, Jum, Annie's, etc.) auto-create on YOUR one AliExpress account
You batch-pay them once a day
AliExpress ships directly to each customer
Store owners never touch AliExpress — they just see orders + tracking in their dashboard
Store owners don't pay anything except their $19.99/month subscription. They set the retail price, you handle the supply chain. That's the whole dropshipping model — you're the platform operator.

The profit split:

Customer pays: $16.72
AliExpress cost: ~$5.00
ToGoGo commission (5%): ~$0.84
Store owner keeps: ~$10.88
The store owner profits without ever touching a supplier. You profit from the 5% commission on every sale across every store. Everyone wins.

Everyone profits. But the problem is — the AliExpress feed API returns ~US$3.80 as the "cost," not the A$12.88 you actually pay. The real cost is roughly 3.4x higher than what the API says.

So a shoe showing A$60.96 on the store means:

API sale price: ~A$30.48
2x markup: A$60.96
Real AE cost (probably): ~A$40-45
Profit: ~A$16-20
Your 30%: ~A$5-6
Store owner: ~A$10-14
Want me to change it to exactly 1.5x? Prices would drop to ~A$45 for that shoe, but you might lose money if the real AE cost is higher than the API price.

Smart call. Cancel the duplicates and the new 4 orders. Don't pay for anything at the wrong price.

The pattern is clear now:

API product price + shipping (~US$0-2) + tax (~15-20%) = real cost
Real cost is roughly 2-3x the API product price
So the multiplier needs to be at least 3.5-4x on the API price to break even + profit. With your 1.5x markup on the REAL cost, that means:

Real cost = API price × 2.5 (covers shipping + tax + conversion)
Store price = real cost × 1.5
Total multiplier: API price × 3.75
Want me to set it to 4x and re-import? That would make:

Bag (API A$1.67): store price A$6.68 (real cost ~A$3.50, profit ~A$3.18)

Actually — even 4x might not be enough for some items. The pricing problem won't be fully solved with any single multiplier because shipping varies per product.

arent these costs in thier api call



Good question! Let me check — the product details API already returns shipping costs:


Searched code
Searched code

Yes! The product details API returns shippingFee per shipping method. But the feed API (used for bulk import) doesn't include shipping.

The fix: during import, after getting the product from the feed, fetch shipping cost for each product and add it to the cost base. But that's slow — one API call per product.

Shipping: ~US$2 (~A$3)
Tax: ~18% of product price
Total cost = (API price × 1.18) + A$3
Store price = total cost × 1.5

What is ship_to_days?ship_to_days is a field that appears mainly in AliExpress Affiliate APIs (for promoters/dropshippers) and some seller backend tools.It tells you:The estimated delivery time to a specific country when using that shipping method.
Format example: "ship to AU in 7 days" or "ship to RU in 10 days".

It usually combines:The destination country (e.g. AU for Australia)
The number of days it typically takes to arrive

This field is especially useful for free shipping listings because:Many products show "Free Shipping" but still have different speed levels.
A lower ship_to_days number (like 7 or 10) means the seller is using a faster free shipping method (e.g. Cainiao Super Economy, AliExpress Standard Shipping, or ePacket-style).
Higher numbers (20–60+ days) usually mean slower free shipping (like China Post or basic economy).

Why it matters for FREE SHIPPINGFree Shipping ≠ Fast Shipping.
ship_to_days helps you quickly see how long the free option will actually take to your country (Australia in your case).
Sellers sometimes offer multiple shipping options: one is "Free" with longer days, and paid ones with fewer days.
In affiliate tools or product data exports, this field is used to filter "fast free shipping" products.

On the normal AliExpress website/app (not API)You won't always see the exact text "ship_to_days", but you will see similar info:Under the product → Shipping tab
It shows "Delivery: X–Y days" or "Free shipping to Australia in about Z days"
Look for the "Fast Delivery" or "Choice" badges — these usually have lower days.

If you're using affiliate links, product scrapers, or tools like DSers/ZenDrop, this ship_to_days field often appears in the raw data.Quick tips for Australia (AU)Good free shipping: 7–15 days is decent nowadays.
Excellent: under 10 days (rare for true free, but possible with some sellers).
Avoid if you need it fast: anything over 20–25 days on free shipping.

Do you want me to explain:How to find fast free shipping products on AliExpress?
What the different shipping methods mean?
Or are you working with the Affiliate API and need help reading the endpoints/fields?

Searching the web

38 results

Yes, this is a very common frustration when working with AliExpress items (especially in dropshipping or affiliate setups).The API price you get is usually the base product price (often in USD, without location-specific adjustments).
When your customer goes to the real AliExpress checkout (or when you place the order), the price jumps because of:Shipping cost (depends on the method chosen — free shipping often shows low ship_to_days but can still have hidden costs or slower options)
Tax / GST (for Australia it's 10%, and AliExpress must collect it on most orders now)
Sometimes platform fees, currency conversion, or dynamic pricing based on the buyer's country/IP

You mentioned +18% — that could be 10% GST + extra shipping + possible small duty/handling on certain items. In 2026, AliExpress has tightened tax collection and some shipping rules, so surprises at checkout happen more often.How to show your customers the final all-in price like Temu doesTemu shows one clean price because they control the entire supply chain and bundle shipping + GST into the displayed price. AliExpress is a marketplace, so it's harder — but you can get close with these practical methods:Best & Most Accurate Way (Recommended for dropshipping)
Use a dropshipping tool or AliExpress integration app that calculates the real final cost in real time:Popular tools: DSers, AutoDS, CJdropshipping, Zendrop, or AliDropship.
These tools let you import the product, then show your customers a markup price that already includes:Your profit margin
Estimated shipping (based on current rates to Australia)
10% GST

Many of them pull live shipping options (including ship_to_days data) and let you set rules like "add X% for tax + shipping buffer".

Using AliExpress Official APIs (if you're technical) Affiliate API: Good for product data and ship_to_days, but shipping/tax calculation is limited.
Dropshipper / Logistics API: There are endpoints like aliexpress.logistics.shipping.get or similar that can return shipping costs to a specific country (e.g., AU) for a product.
You can combine:Base price from product API
Shipping cost from logistics/shipping API (for the chosen method)
Add 10% GST on (product price + shipping)

Then display: Base + Shipping + GST = Final Price

This requires development work and an approved AliExpress developer account.
Simple Manual / Rule-Based Approach (Quick to implement) For free shipping items (low ship_to_days like 7–15 days to AU):Add a fixed buffer: e.g. +12–18% on the API price (covers GST + average shipping variance).
Or break it down: API price × 1.10 (GST) + $3–8 fixed shipping estimate.

Show your customer:
"Final price including GST & shipping to Australia: $XX.XX"
(with a small disclaimer: "Estimated – actual may vary slightly at checkout")
For paid shipping items: Pull the cheapest shipping option manually or via tool and add it.

Pro Tips to Make It Closer to Temu ExperiencePrioritize AliExpress Choice items with fast free shipping (often better ship_to_days and more predictable costs).
Test real orders from an Australian address to see the exact difference between API price and final checkout.
On your site, clearly state: "Price includes estimated shipping & Australian GST. You pay this amount when we fulfill via AliExpress."
Offer free shipping on your store for orders over a certain amount (absorb the cost in your margin).

Recommendations for the easiest dropshipping app that handles this automatically?
Or examples of how much buffer people usually add (e.g., 15–20%)?

Just tell me your setup (e.g. Shopify/WooCommerce, custom site, affiliate only, etc.) and I can give more precise steps. This way you can compete better with Temu's "what you see is what you pay" feel.

Here's exactly how to handle your situation based on the real example you shared:Subtotal: US $7.60
Shipping: Free shipping
Tax: US $0.96
Total: US $8.56 This is a classic AliExpress checkout breakdown for Australia.
The API gives you the subtotal ($7.60), but at checkout AliExpress adds:Tax = roughly 12.6% here ($0.96 on $7.60)
(It's supposed to be 10% GST, but in practice it often comes out higher because AliExpress calculates GST on the subtotal + shipping value or before certain discounts. Many Australian buyers notice 12–18% effective tax on cheap items.)

Your goal: Show customers a single final price (like Temu) so they don't get a surprise jump at checkout.Recommended Simple & Practical Formula (for Australia)For items with Free Shipping (like your example):Final Price to show customer = API Subtotal × 1.18
(or round up slightly for safety)Why 18%?Covers the ~10–13% GST you actually see at checkout
Adds a small buffer for currency conversion, minor shipping variations, or platform fees
Gives you room for your profit margin

Applying it to your example:API price: $7.60
× 1.18 = US $8.97 (or round to $8.99 / $9.00 for nice pricing)

This is very close to the real total of $8.56. You absorb a tiny difference or make it up in margin.Better Breakdown Approach (More Transparent)Show your customers this on the product page:Price: US $8.99
Includes:Product: $7.60
Shipping: Free
Australian GST & fees: Included
Total you pay: $8.99

Add a small note:
"Final price including estimated shipping & 10% GST to Australia. We fulfill via AliExpress."How to Implement This on Your StoreQuick & Easy (No/Low Code) Use a dropshipping app like DSers, AutoDS, or Zopi — they have built-in pricing rules.
You can set: "Add 18% to all AliExpress prices" or "Add 10% GST + fixed buffer".
Some apps (like Shipify + DSers) can even pull live shipping rates per product.

If You're Using Custom Code / API Take the product API price (subtotal)
Add logic:
final_price = api_price * 1.10 (for GST)
final_price = final_price + shipping_estimate (even if "free", add $0.50–$2 buffer)
final_price = final_price * 1.05 (small safety + your margin)
Or just hardcode × 1.15 to 1.20 for free-shipping items to Australia.

Pro Tips for 2026Focus on AliExpress Choice or items with good ship_to_days (7–15 days to AU) — these tend to have more predictable "free shipping" and lower surprises.
Test a few real orders from an Australian address to see the exact tax % on your products (it varies by item price and seller).
For very cheap items (< $5–10), the % markup often feels higher — consider bundling or minimum order value.

No please stay on this branch and yes figure out the real shipping cost, i know you said it would be slower, like what do you mean by that? slower downloading there items into our database? or in another way?



Good question! The "slower" only affects the import process (background), NOT the customer experience:

Current (fast import):

Feed API → 50 products in 1 call (~2 seconds)
Apply formula, save to DB
Done — but prices are estimates
Accurate (slower import):

Feed API → 50 products in 1 call (~2 seconds)
Then for EACH product, call getProductDetails() to get shipping cost to AU
50 extra API calls × ~1-2 seconds each = ~60-100 seconds extra
But prices are accurate
The customer never notices — they see instant prices from the database either way. The slowness is only during the background import, which runs via cron every 6 hours.

The issue is Vercel's 10-second timeout on serverless functions. So we either:

Process fewer products per run (10-15 instead of 100) — import takes more runs but prices are accurate
Keep the two-step approach — fast import first, then run enrich endpoint to fix prices
Which do you prefer? Option 1 is cleaner — every product has accurate pricing from the start. Option 2 means products show estimated prices until enriched.

so like this if have shipping costs we add to the price + the tax then that = our wholesale price for TOGOGO, then on our Client Store, they get our whole sale Price + 1.5x their commission my our 30% togogo fee, but then on checkout all Orders get a $6.00 shipping fee that goes to TOGOGO, does this make sense?



Makes perfect sense. Here's the flow:

1. Import (with real shipping):

wholesale_cost = API_price + AE_shipping + AE_tax(~18%)
sale_price = wholesale_cost × 1.5

2. At checkout:

Customer pays: sale_price + A$6 shipping
ToGoGo gets: 30% of profit + A$6 shipping
Store owner gets: sale_price - 30% commission

Example (flashlight):

API price: US$2.77 → ~A$4.16
AE shipping: US$1.99 → ~A$2.99
AE tax: ~A$0.75
Wholesale cost: A$7.90
Store price (1.5x): A$11.85
Customer pays: A$11.85 + A$6 = A$17.85
Profit: A$3.95
ToGoGo: A$1.19 (30%) + A$6 shipping = A$7.19
Store owner: A$2.76
Let me build it. The import will be slower (10-15 products per run) but every price will be accurate.

1 step
I want to know if u pay extra shipping for larger items?



Yes — larger/heavier items can have US$3-5+ shipping on AliExpress.

The good news: our code already handles this. It uses whichever is higher — the API shipping cost or the A$3 minimum:

actualShipping = Math.max(API shipping × 1.45, A$3.00)

So:

Small item: API says FREE → we use A$3.00
Large item: API says US$4.50 → we use A$6.53 (4.50 × 1.45)
The risk is the same as the FREE problem — the API might underreport shipping on big items too. Only way to know for sure is to test buy some larger items and compare.

Want to check a specific large item? Use the price-check endpoint with its product ID and we can compare.

Yes, congrats on getting your TOGOGO.ME one-click store setup fully working with AliExpress API integration, Stripe payments, and subdomains—that's a solid achievement! Sounds like a smooth dropshipping flow now.AliExpress Rewards, Coupons, and Discounts for DropshippersAliExpress does offer various discounts, coupons, promotions, coins, and rewards (like cashback or loyalty perks), but they're primarily designed for regular retail buyers or high-volume dropshippers buying directly on the platform. Here's the realistic breakdown for your use case (as a platform owner passing value to your end customers):Standard buyer coupons and site-wide promotions: These include seller-specific coupons, store coupons, AliExpress-wide promo codes, flash sales, Choice Day deals, and coin-based discounts. Dropshippers (you or your automated system) can often access and apply many of these when placing orders manually or via tools like browser extensions/Chrome helpers. Some dropshipping apps (e.g., DSers) even have built-in features to scan and apply available AliExpress coupons automatically to your fulfillment orders.

help.dsers.com

Dropshipping-specific perks (AliExpress Dropshipping Center / Business account): If you register a free AliExpress Business/Dropshipping account (and especially if you hit volume thresholds), you can unlock tiered discounts on your purchases (e.g., up to 6% off based on total spend levels like $5k+ for Level A). There are also "Exclusive DS Price" items and occasional incentives/coupons for verified dropshippers. This reduces your cost, which you could then use to offer better pricing or occasional promos to your customers. Some plugins/partners even provide extra bonuses or coupons when you order through them.

easync.io

Rewards/coins/cashback: Regular buyers earn coins through activities, which act like discounts on future orders. Cashback services or extensions can add more savings on the buyer side. These aren't directly "for dropshippers" in a programmatic way, but high-volume accounts or certain tools can benefit indirectly.

Can You Pass These On to Your Customers?Not directly or automatically in a seamless way for every order, for a few reasons:Your setup uses the AliExpress API to pull products and handle fulfillment. Most API-based order placement (common in automated dropshipping) bypasses the normal checkout page where many dynamic coupons, coins, or buyer-specific discounts are applied. Coupons that work great on the AliExpress website often don't carry over cleanly to API orders.

reddit.com

Coupons are frequently buyer-account specific, time-limited, or tied to the shopping session on AliExpress.com. Your customers aren't logging into AliExpress themselves—they're buying from your subdomain store. You (or your system) place the order on their behalf using your supplier account/details.
Seller coupons (from individual AliExpress sellers) can sometimes be applied, but they vary per product/seller and aren't guaranteed. Tools exist to extract them, but automation depends on your exact integration.

That said, you can still pass on value in practical ways:Lower your costs and build in better margins/pricing — Use any dropshipper discounts, volume tiers, or coupon tools on your end to reduce what you pay AliExpress. Then price your store competitively (or run your own sales/discount codes via your platform). This effectively "passes on" savings without needing to share AliExpress codes.
Manual or semi-automated coupon hunting — For high-value orders or promotions, monitor AliExpress deals and apply them when fulfilling. Some third-party tools/extensions help find and stack coupons (e.g., coupon finders that pop up at checkout).
Your own rewards program — Since you control the storefront (subdomains, Stripe, etc.), build loyalty features directly: referral discounts, first-purchase codes, bundle deals, or membership rewards. This is often more effective and brandable than trying to proxy AliExpress perks. Many successful dropshippers do this instead of relying on supplier coupons.
Affiliate angle — AliExpress has an affiliate program (up to ~9% commission on referred sales, with product feeds and tracking). You could promote specific products via affiliate links if it fits your model, but it doesn't directly help with passing discounts to your direct customers (it's more for earning extra on traffic you send to AliExpress).

best-affiliate-marketing-programs.com

Recommendations for Your TOGOGO.ME SetupCheck if your current AliExpress API integration supports any coupon/ discount parameters (look in the API docs for order creation endpoints—some have fields for promotions).
Consider registering for the official AliExpress Dropshipping Center if you haven't—it’s geared exactly for this and can give you better visibility into DS-specific pricing and tools.
Test with tools like coupon extractors or apps that integrate with AliExpress for dropshipping—they often make applying available discounts easier on the fulfillment side.
For passing savings: Focus on your platform's features. Offer "limited-time deals" or "member discounts" that you fund from your margin. It's cleaner legally and for customer experience (no confusion about AliExpress branding in your store).

If you run into limitations with the API not capturing certain promos, many dropshippers simply absorb small variations or occasionally fulfill manually during big sales events to capture extra discounts.If you share more details about how your product import/ordering flow works (e.g., which exact API methods or any middleware you're using), or if you've tried applying coupons already, I can dig deeper into specifics. Have you set up an AliExpress Business account yet? That could be a quick win for extra perks on your volume.
